  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_14f92180-d9b1-49fe-ab3f-b4f458167dad'

<span id="freeTextContainer10557831803248380026">Roland and his tet have just returned to the path of the Beam when they discover that they are being followed by a group of inexperienced trackers. The trackers are from the town of Calla Bryn Sturgis, and they desperately need the help of gunslingers. Once every generation, a band of masked riders known as the Wolves gallop out of the dark land of Thunderclap to steal one</span>
  <span id="freeText10557831803248380026" style="display:none">Roland and his tet have just returned to the path of the Beam when they discover that they are being followed by a group of inexperienced trackers. The trackers are from the town of Calla Bryn Sturgis, and they desperately need the help of gunslingers. Once every generation, a band of masked riders known as the Wolves gallop out of the dark land of Thunderclap to steal one half of all the twins born in the Callas. When the children are returned, they are roont, or mentally and physically ruined. In less than a month, the Wolves will raid again. In exchange for Roland’s aid, Father Callahan—a priest originally from our world—offers to give Roland a powerful but evil seeing sphere, a sinister globe called Black Thirteen which he has hidden below the floorboards of his church. Not only must Roland and his tet discover a way to defeat the invincible Wolves, but they must also return to New York so that they can save our world’s incarnation of the Dark Tower from the machinations of the evil Sombra Corporation.</span>

<div id="review_6595558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595558" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6595558?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/656420.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=alt-universes">alt-universes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2011-r">2011-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6595558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5027961240286823422">If someone would have told me back in the ‘90s that the way to get Stephen King to finish up the <i>Dark Tower</i> series quickly was to hit him with a minivan, I would have been on my way to Maine to rent a Dodge Caravan before you could say, "Bango Skank was here."<br/><br/>I confess this not to do more complaining about the long suffering years waiting on some advancement in the <i>Dark Tower</i> books, but to illustrate how utterly obsessed and frustrated I was with this goddamn series. Then King nearly came to the</span>
  <span id="freeText5027961240286823422" style="display:none">If someone would have told me back in the ‘90s that the way to get Stephen King to finish up the <i>Dark Tower</i> series quickly was to hit him with a minivan, I would have been on my way to Maine to rent a Dodge Caravan before you could say, "Bango Skank was here."<br /><br />I confess this not to do more complaining about the long suffering years waiting on some advancement in the <i>Dark Tower</i> books, but to illustrate how utterly obsessed and frustrated I was with this goddamn series. Then King nearly came to the clearing at the end of the path but instead recovered and cranked out three books like they came off an assembly line to finish the whole thing. Before that, I had pretty much given up hope on ever getting another book, never mind seeing an end to it, and King wasn’t doing much to make me change my mind with no news about him even working on another <i>DT</i> book.<br /><br />And then came the minivan. <br /><br />Ka works in mysterious ways….<br /><br /><i>Wolves of the Calla</i> had a lot of things to accomplish. It needed to get the story rolling again after years of it laying fallow. It needed to set up the end run of the series. It needed to be a satisfying book aside from moving the overall arc forward. And most importantly, it needed to answer the burning question all <i>Dark Tower</i> fans had: Whatever happened to Father Callahan from <i>‘Salem’s Lot</i>? Oh, wait. I had never asked that question. Oh, well. I found out anyhow and it turned out to be a pretty good part of the story.<br /><br />Roland and his crew have been moving along the path of the Beam towards the Tower, but they seem to have been in a kind of timeless funk. (One of the things I love about the series is that the decay of the Tower has caused both time and space in Roland’s world to become soft and drift. It’s also a nice metaphor for the limbo that characters are in between books.) Just before entering the nastiness of End-World, they find Calla Bryn Sturgis, a farming town with a big problem.<br /><br />Almost all the children born in the Calla are twins. Every twenty years or so, dozens of creatures the townsfolk call Wolves come on horseback and steal one from each set of twins. They take those kids back to Thunderclap, a place the gunslingers have already been warned about, and eventually return them as almost mindless husks who grow to jumbo sizes before dying young. Try to fight or hide your kids, and the Wolves kill everyone who resists instead of just taking half the kids. The Wolves will arrive in a month, but some in the Calla want to fight back this time if the gunslingers will help. <br /><br />Roland's group has other problems too. They’ve been making dream-like excursions to New York in the 1970s and found that the special rose growing in a vacant lot there is in terrible danger. The rose is a key manifestation of the Tower in that world. Roland is convinced that if the rose is destroyed, the Tower falls in his world, too, and there goes your ballgame for all of existence. They have to find a way to get to New York in person and save the rose from those threatening it by protecting the owner of the lot.<br /><br />The gunslingers also meet Callahan, a former Catholic priest last seen in the King-verse fighting vampires in <i>’Salem’s Lot</i>. Callahan has an incredible tale to tell of years spent traveling between worlds and being chased by vampires and other nasty agents of the Crimson King before he wound up in Calla Bryn Sturgis.* Callahan has been hiding an evil object that terrifies him, and he wants Roland to get rid of it by taking it with him when they leave.<br /><br /><i>*(Anyone reading the series who wants some more info about who was chasing Callahan and other bits that come into play here should check out King’s ‘Low Men in Yellow Coats’ story in his ‘Hearts in Atlantis’ collection.)</i><br /><br />If they didn’t have enough on their plate, Susannah’s previous encounter with a demon has left her a little bit pregnant, and her personality is being taken over by the baby’s ‘mother’, Mia. Pregnant women are known for strange food cravings, but let’s just say that Mia’s are even worse than usual.<br /><br />I love this book partly because it’s the one that got the <i>Dark Tower</i> story back on track and set up everything for the end run to the last book. I also love it just because this is <i>Dark Tower</i> at its best for me. It’s a mash-up of westerns, fantasy, horror and sci-fi. It’s like <i>The Magnificent Seven</i> if Yul Brenner and Steve McQueen had to make multi-dimensional trips and deal with robots and vampires as well as protect the town with their six-guns.<br /><br />Another thing I like about this one is that Eddie, Susannah and Jake are now full-fledged gunslingers and not just apprentices, and King expands on exactly what a gunslinger is. They’re not just killers, although they do that pretty damn well. They’re also diplomats and protectors of the defenseless. It was fun to see Roland’s manipulative political side come out when dealing with the Calla folk. The pregnancy storyline didn’t do much for me in this, but it becomes a key driver of the plot of the next book.<br /><br />All in all, this is one of my favorite of the <i>DT</i> books, and it was King’s clear statement that he was done screwing around and ready to finish this mother. Too bad it took him nearly getting killed to get it done.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5027961240286823422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2320519488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320519488" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320519488?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=king-stephen">king-stephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320519488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7734761276345556885">Come, just stroke them, they won´t lacerate you and if, it will be so immediately fatal that you will at least feel no pain, except if bitten by a blue glowing vampire before, that could complicate both the dying and getting all the pop culture references and innuendos.<br/><br/>It´s getting a bit complicated with all the interconnections to the other parts, but King does a great job by using new and established settings, symbols, and artifacts to keep it suspenseful and demanding to read at the same time</span>
  <span id="freeText7734761276345556885" style="display:none">Come, just stroke them, they won´t lacerate you and if, it will be so immediately fatal that you will at least feel no pain, except if bitten by a blue glowing vampire before, that could complicate both the dying and getting all the pop culture references and innuendos.<br /><br />It´s getting a bit complicated with all the interconnections to the other parts, but King does a great job by using new and established settings, symbols, and artifacts to keep it suspenseful and demanding to read at the same time. There is no of his works or series with a similar emphasis on fusing it all together with as many character lines and mentioned elements, there are works taking place at the same or similar setting or with the same characters such as The Shining or the Mr. Mercedes series, but nothing close to this.<br /><br />Look forward to one of the creepiest, best demonic possession scenes ever.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The setting surrounding Mia is so creepy, I mean, I am a man and I can luckily not give birth, because I wouldn´t survive it, weak as I am, but I imagine reading it as a mother so terrifying that I couldn´t find a name for it. Perverting the symbol of love, the reason to live, the essence of life to breeding the freaking antichrist, playing with the most essential element of human relationship on such nerve wracking claviatures of terror is ingenious.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This scenery, allocated to different parts of the series, is one of the best King has ever written, it won´t ever leave your memory again, even if you wish, scream, and plead for it, it will haunt you until after the grave, each new incarnation, and yes, it may be you who it is. Try to handle that, getting reborn as: see spoiler.<br /><br />It´s not just that King is referring to his own work, characters, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he even integrates himself, I mean how cool is this? He is caricaturing himself and his weaknesses, something one needs much self- reflection and self-criticism for  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and many are unable to because they deem themselves so over the top. <br /><br />This part is essential for understanding the whole deeper meaning King integrated into his work and I couldn´t name all the innuendos and especially the interconnectivity floating through this series, but I am not sure if some parts are not just over the top philosophy and glitter or if King was, next to his literary ingenuity, also so clever to add so much second lawyer under the skin of the story.<br /><br />How I loved this creepy setting, the mutations, some Sci-Fi elements with open questions fermenting in the background, the good oldfashioned <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[handle me kids each whatever melodramatic time period I choose or… <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the explanation of the backstory,… it has everything. <br /><br />And how could I not love an evil megacorp and no, this time I won´t start driveling about how cool it would have been if King would have written more Sci-Fi…oopsie. However, I would have loved to have seen more of this element and plot level, because King has everything else, the standard crew, check, the personified evil and the meta evil, check, but what is kind of missing is the evil mega conglomerate that is once not tinkering with alien technology or invasive alien species, but with the dark side itself. <br /><br />A stronger focus on this aspect would have made it even more dynamic, but King prefers to show the evil characters, not the evil ideologies, but I imagine an evil parallel universe where he might have written it this way as part of a historic nonfiction book. Because, the saddest thing of this dystopic uchronia, he wouldn´t have been allowed to work in forbidden creative jobs and would have had to work as propaganda indoctrination demagogue black magic somewhat teacher instead. Sigh, if I could just have been in one of his classes, possibly necromancy or mind control by demonic possession, it would have rocked so much…<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/WolvesOfTheCalla">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_151903964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151903964" />
    <a title="Rhiannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5071150-rhiannon"><img alt="Rhiannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302016584p2/5071150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151903964?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhiannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhiannon" href="/user/show/5071150-rhiannon">Rhiannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of westerns, masochists</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rhiannon by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5098735-uwdave">Uwdave</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=end-of-the-world">end-of-the-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151903964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14491086001690511856">It is as though Stephen King:<br/>1. Took me out to an arid, deserted sepia-toned no-place<br/>2. Lit a sputtering campfire that quickly faded to embers<br/>3. Handcuffed me<br/>4. Sat me down Indian-style across from him<br/>5. Proceeded to narrate to me in a hoarse, bored drawl over a series of three-to-four weeks the world's longest, most uninteresting story while my head lolled back, my lips grew dry with thirst, and my bum ached<br/><br/>If this book had been written by any writer other than Stephen King, it would never have</span>
  <span id="freeText14491086001690511856" style="display:none">It is as though Stephen King:<br />1. Took me out to an arid, deserted sepia-toned no-place<br />2. Lit a sputtering campfire that quickly faded to embers<br />3. Handcuffed me<br />4. Sat me down Indian-style across from him<br />5. Proceeded to narrate to me in a hoarse, bored drawl over a series of three-to-four weeks the world's longest, most uninteresting story while my head lolled back, my lips grew dry with thirst, and my bum ached<br /><br />If this book had been written by any writer other than Stephen King, it would never have been published. I firmly believe that an editor, or any discerning eye, never even glanced at this book.<br /><br />I will say that the only redeeming storyline in this entire book is Don (Pere) Callahan's tale. In it, King writes some surprisingly beautiful prose. Callahan's tale - which is interspersed throughout the main storyline - moves in a pace that a story like this <em>should</em> move - like hurried steps on a Manhattan sidewalk, like a nervous glance backward as though someone might be following you. Because guess what? Someone <em>is</em> following you - me, the reader! And if I'm following your little ka-tet through the boring, desolate redneck wonderland of the Calla for 925 freakin' pages - you better move! However, how much does Callahan's story actually move the plot? Very little. It seems to serve two purposes: to reinforce coincidence as "ka," and as an example of the quality of writing of which King is capable, but which you, reader, are being denied throughout the rest of the narrative. <br /><br />Besides the sheer grueling pace of this beast, I had a couple of serious problems with this particular book in the Dark Tower Series:<br /><br />1. Speech Mannerisms: The language of the Calla is annoying. When Roland's ka-tet continue to use these annoying speech mannerisms in their own "palaver" - it comes off as completely ridiculous. Not to mention - exhausting for the reader.<br /><br />2. Repetition: Certain tropes (Nineteen, for example) are repeated too often. It is bad writing, simply put. While I do not yet understand the "significance" of Nineteen, it has been implied that it is significant. <em>So, so significant.</em> Yawn.<br /><br />3. Mia: Susannah already has three personalities. Giving her another one is simply a rehashing and reheating of King's own once-interesting characterizations. <br /><br />So, if the pace is slow, the plot overdrawn, surely in 925 pages there is room for some serious character development, right? Wrong! Besides Jake Chambers doing a little "coming of age," the rest of the characters remain stagnant throughout the narrative - to the point where they seem like thoughtless renditions of themselves. Even Mia - <em>a brand new personality!</em> - is derivative of Susannah's older personalities and is largely uninteresting.<br /><br />I will also say that I find the subplot of the Callahan's meta-fiction interesting. I find it easy to believe that a quest that traverses time/place/universes, can surely traverse the border between reality and fiction. This development of a fiction-bridging reality could be spectacular if done correctly. Or it could fall off, and go nowhere. I cannot say I have faith for the former. <br /><br />My enjoyment of Callahan's tale is the only reason I gave this book more than one star. <br /><br />That said - I won't give up now. Not with thousands of pages of this series already read. I mean, I have to get to that Tower. But, God, God God - I want to give up. God, this Wolves of The Calla book was long. I felt like I was reading it for nineteen years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14491086001690511856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_14801062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14801062" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14801062?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/656420.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=reread-in-2011">reread-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=weird-western">weird-western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14801062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12152557489247967662"><b>The 2011 re-read:</b><br/>Roland and his ka-tet of gunslingers ride into Calla Bryn Sturgis, a town with a problem. Once every generation, a gang of marauders called The Wolves ride out of Thunderclap and steal half of the town's children. The ones that return come back roont, or brain-damaged. Can Roland and the others stop the Wolves before Susan gives birth to the demon in her womb?<br/><br/>It was a long wait between Wizard and Glass and Wolves of the Calla. Was it worth it? Well, does a horse piss where it pl</span>
  <span id="freeText12152557489247967662" style="display:none"><b>The 2011 re-read:</b><br />Roland and his ka-tet of gunslingers ride into Calla Bryn Sturgis, a town with a problem. Once every generation, a gang of marauders called The Wolves ride out of Thunderclap and steal half of the town's children. The ones that return come back roont, or brain-damaged. Can Roland and the others stop the Wolves before Susan gives birth to the demon in her womb?<br /><br />It was a long wait between Wizard and Glass and Wolves of the Calla. Was it worth it? Well, does a horse piss where it pleases?<br /><br />The main story of Wolves of the Calla is right out of The Magnificent Seven or Seven Samurai. The gunslingers ride into town, prepare the town, and settle the bad guys' hash. The secondary stories, of which there are several, are what make the book. You've got Father Callahan from Jake, Eddie, and Susannah's world and his fearsome burden, Black Thirteen. You've got someone in town helping the Wolves. You've got Roland and his arthritis. You've got Calvin Tower and the vacant lot containing the Rose. And most of all, you have Susannah's disturbing pregnancy.<br /><br />The gang going todash was one of the more interesting parts of the book and something I'd forgotten about in the years since I read this book the first time. I devoured the book in a day and a half when it first came out so I must not have savored it. There were so many wrinkles to the story that I'd forgotten.<br /><br />I love how the Man in Black doubled back and met Callahan at the Way Station while Roland and Jake were on in trail in The Gunslinger. In the revised edition of The Gunslinger, Roland contemplates putting his quest on hold for a few years and training Jake so he'd have another Gunslinger with him. Would they have met Callahan if they'd let the Man in Black get away? Tantalizing...<br /><br />People say that the long flashback in Wizard and Glass fleshed out Roland's personality. I'd say watching Roland interact with the people of Calla Bryn Sturgis in this book went a lot farther in showing what kind of man Roland was before the world moved on.<br /><br />I can't really say much more for fear of giving too many things away to people who have never read it. If you like the Dark Tower, this one is probably in the top three books of the series.<br /><br /><b>The 2019 re-read:</b><br />I've been meaning to re-read books 5-7 of the Dark Tower for a few years now. When my wife and I found out we were having a chap, I put it on my 2019 reading goals and here we are. My original intention was to read all three before little Miles tears my wife's loins in two but I'm not sure how motivated I am to do that.<br /><br />The story itself, the ka-tet defending a village from mysterious raiders who steal one of each pair of twins in the village every generation or so, is as compelling now as when I read it hot off the presses. As with the 2011 reread, I'd forgotten quite a bit about this book.<br /><br />It's probably because this is my third go-round but the things that irk me are a lot more apparent than in previous reads. This book could easily be at least 100 pages shorter. Wolves of the Calla suffers from a case of King Bloat in the middle. There's so much talking when the ka-tet could be going to New York to save the Rose! "I know time flows one and a half times as fast on the New York side of things and Balazar's goons are putting the squeeze on Calvin Tower but let's stay up all night and listen to Pere Callahan's story some more." The Calla-speak gets really painful after a while.<br /><br />Now that the gripes are out of the way, I still dug this book and The Dark Tower as a whole. The todash concept is great and Stephen King knows how to ratchet up the suspense when he needs to. Parts of it were still surprising, even though I've trod this path twice before. The final battle with the Wolves was some tense shit, even though I knew the ka-tet would survive, I couldn't remember which of the townsfolk died.<br /><br />While a bit of the shine has worn off this penny, I still enjoyed Wolves of the Call quite a bit. 4 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12152557489247967662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/656420.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641303948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18359761080503400659">"Now I think that all of us are born with a hole in our hearts, and we go around looking for the person who can fill it. You...Eddie, you fill me up."<br/><br/>The fifth book in the Dark Tower series finds Roland and his ka-tet in Calla Bryn Sturgis, where they must help the residents overcome a formidable enemy.<br/><br/>Even though this book took me what felt like a million years to finish, I thoroughly enjoyed pretty much every page (well... I’m not the biggest fan of the New York plot in this one, I’d rather ha</span>
  <span id="freeText18359761080503400659" style="display:none">"Now I think that all of us are born with a hole in our hearts, and we go around looking for the person who can fill it. You...Eddie, you fill me up."<br /><br />The fifth book in the Dark Tower series finds Roland and his ka-tet in Calla Bryn Sturgis, where they must help the residents overcome a formidable enemy.<br /><br />Even though this book took me what felt like a million years to finish, I thoroughly enjoyed pretty much every page (well... I’m not the biggest fan of the New York plot in this one, I’d rather have just stayed in the Calla!)<br /><br />King is well-known for his depiction of small towns and bringing all the residents to life, and this one is no different! Lots of new characters to meet, as well as the reintroduction of an old one. I LOVED catching up with this character, quite a lot of time is spent filling in the gaps of his story and I was not complaining in the slightest!<br /><br />The Dark Tower is such an epic tale where our ka-tet are mostly travelling around and on the move, so I liked just staying still for a while (apart from going todash) and allowing for more character development. Also a huge fan of the story behind the wolves and the roont children - I find it creepily fascinating!<br /><br />I fangirl so hard over all the little references to pop culture and connections to other King books etc so I was in my element here! I guess not everyone enjoys that kind of stuff, but this gal does! And if you haven’t read the series before, this one ends in a way where you just NEED to know what happens next. But luckily I have so I’m okay waiting to read Song of Susannah - however, not for too long, because the Tower is beckoning...<br /><br />An underrated DT novel, in my opinion. 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18359761080503400659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1535417525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535417525" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1535417525?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535417525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4982814026821522963"><br/><br/><b>Commela Come Come!</b><br/><br/>Our journey has left so many behind. We have been attacked, beaten, and threatened. Yet, we persevere.   <span id="freeText4982814026821522963" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>Commela Come Come!</b><br /><br />Our journey has left so many behind. We have been attacked, beaten, and threatened. Yet, we persevere. Onward wayward travelers. Let us continue on our quest to the <b>Dark Tower</b>. Let us travel safely along <i>the Path of the Beam</i><br /><br />Our band of crazy MahFahs, led by the craziest MahFah yeh’ve ever encountered- Yours Truly- has seen and done much. I even let Jeff out of his <s>prison</s> luxiourous bedroom at my home to join us in this read. I did keep him on a leash- he’s not to be trusted.<br /><br />Back to the review:<br /><br />Roland and his Tet are on the Path of the Beam in search of the Dark Tower. After surviving the Starkblast and hearing another story from Roland’s past the gang is ready to move forward. But they’re being watched by the folken of the Calla. Which Calla? Calla Bryn Sturgis.<br /><br />As much as Roland’s Tet would love to take a different route, Roland explains to them why they can’t. The duty of the gunslinger is to stand for those who cannot. Stand and be true, aye. He says true. What they find in the Calla is horrifying. Wolves come on horseback once every 26 years to take one from every set of twins. In our world that might not be so bad- but in the Calla twins are as common as Canadian pennies in a handful of change. <br /><br />What’s worse than that? The wolves send them back once they’re done with them and that twin is forever ROONT; a drooling buffoon capable** of mostly just grunts and giggles.<br /><br />One of my favorite characters became a favorite because of this book- Pere Callahan. His story in Salem’s Lot was not finished. It is continued here in the Calla. <br /><br />Calla. Callahan. <br /><br />But will the other folken listen to his pleas? Can they be convinced that now is the time to stop the wolves? Will Jeff ever get out of my basement for good?<br /><br />This story is laid out beautifully. You are getting just enough information to keep turning those pages. You’re being teased with information. Your leaders are whispering and even you don’t know what they’re saying. There’s robots, twins, taters and gravy, time travel and talking caves. YERBUGGER.<br /><br />Wolves of the Calla is a great read and is filled with a language that is sure to make any buddy read more interesting. I just can’t wait to continue this journey with my Ka-Tet.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4982814026821522963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16067567373541232181"><i>May it do ya fine.</i> This book did me real fine. <i>Say thank ya.</i><br/><br/>I must be picking up the language from Calla Bryn Sturgis/Mid-World because it seems lately, I've been saying the speech of the people. I almost said, "Thankee-sai" as I was handed my receipt today at the grocery store. "Say thankee" I didn't. <br/><br/>Anyways, I'll stop being silly. (The grocery store thing is true, however.)   <span id="freeText16067567373541232181" style="display:none"><i>May it do ya fine.</i> This book did me real fine. <i>Say thank ya.</i><br /><br />I must be picking up the language from Calla Bryn Sturgis/Mid-World because it seems lately, I've been saying the speech of the people. I almost said, "Thankee-sai" as I was handed my receipt today at the grocery store. "Say thankee" I didn't. <br /><br />Anyways, I'll stop being silly. (The grocery store thing is true, however.) What a fan-freaking-tastic book. I really enjoyed the town of Calla Bryn Sturgis, the people, and I LOVED the way they spoke. <br /><br />The story in this volume was just about as great as The Waste Lands....ahem...my favorite installment so far. So, I put this tied with The Drawing of the Three as my second favorite installment. Things were kind of mysterious in some parts, such as who was the snitch, and who or what were the wolves. The end with the 'Salem's Lot mention was also pretty brilliant. Father Callahan's part in the quest for the Dark Tower, the voices at the bottom of the cave, and just all of the connections to the number 19, Calvin Tower, the bookstore, etc....just brilliant.<br /><br />King has such a creative mind, and I think this book completely made up for Wizard and Glass for me. Thanks King for delivering a solid book again. It was real <i>trig. Say thank ya.</i> I won't be surprised if Calla Bryn Sturgis/Mid-World speech is here to stay in my English speech. <br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText669375339514999903" style="display:none"><i>A prequel to a sequel or a sequel to a prequel of a previous Dark Tower “review”.</i><br /><br />Both women’s hands moved like a blur as they obliterated their targets - moving and stationary. Their pistols were still smoking as they were returned them to their holsters.<br /><br />“Well met,” said the fat rancher, as he moved towards the taller of the two women, “and mighty impressive.”<br /><br />“Thankee, Sai”, said the taller of the two blonde katet members and by her calm and authoritative bearing, obviously the group’s dinh.<br /><br />“I’m known as Quick Draw and this here”, indicating her straight shooting partner, “is the Rootin’ Tootin’ Pistol Packin’ one. Her name used to be longer, but folks got confused, so we narrowed it.”<br /><br />“I reckon if yer willin’, we could use yer help against them evil clowns, who’ve been rustlin’ our kittens and turnin’ em into six-legged muties that are lazy and can’t bathe themselves.”<br /><br />“Jenkies! As gunslingers in the Eld tradition, we’d gladly be of service to ya.”<br /><br />The rancher eyed the snoring lump, sleeping face down in the dirt. “If it do ya, can I see the big cully do some shootin?”<br /><br />“He’s a decent shot when he’s sober….” Quick Draw’s voice trailed off.<br /><br />Rootin’ Tootin’ nudged the slumbering figure with her boot, softly at first, but when that didn’t have any effect, she kicked him much harder.<br /><br />“N-O-O-M. that spells moon backwards”, blubbered the hulking figure as he scrambled to his feet.<br /><br />“What in tarnation is he goin’ on bout? Is he one of them roont galoots?<br /><br />"Probably not, sai, he’s sleepin’ off a two day drunk. Or a devil grass bender. We ain’t entirely sure.”<br /><br />She turned toward the blinking, half-asleep man and said, “Kindly, do some shootin’ for us, Jumpin’. There’s a cactus over yonder you can shoot and remember the face of yer father.”<br /><br />“Yer confusin’ me! My daddy could ha’ been the stableman or the deputy or a stuffy guy.”<br /><br />“More than likely the town idjit”, muttered Pistol Packin’.<br /><br />“Jes pick a cactus and shoot.”<br /><br />Jumpin’ shakily raised his pistol and let loose a shot. The shot missed the cactus by a wide margin, ricocheted off a nearby boulder and lodged itself in the fat rancher’s left buttock.<br /><br />“I cry your pardon,” blurted the shooter.<br /><br />As the group behind the rancher started muttering angrily, the two blondes hurriedly grabbed the big man set him on his horse and galloped quickly away ignoring the furious shouts from behind them.<br /><br />“Ka?” came out like a belch from Jumpin’.<br /><br />“I’ll give ya yer fill of ka later,” shouted Quick Draw.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1536022299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1536022299" />
    <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12058788-2"><img alt="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589380555p2/12058788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536022299?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" href="/user/show/12058788-2">Ɗẳɳ  2.☊</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781417645688" href="/book/show/493810.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=western">western</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=when-worlds-collide">when-worlds-collide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=kitten-squishers">kitten-squishers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536022299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13212016721992158456">As my dawdling and ever dwindling ka-tet finally approaches the clearing at the end of the path—praise the Man Jesus—I find myself on the horns of a dilemma. You see, we read Wolves of the Calla nearly a year and a half ago, but I’ve left it unreviewed for a myriad of reasons. Actually . . . no, that’s not entirely true. For some idiotic reason, I began the silly practice of delaying reviews on buddy reads until all, or at least most my friends were finished reading. This delay tactic, commonly </span>
  <span id="freeText13212016721992158456" style="display:none">As my dawdling and ever dwindling ka-tet finally approaches the clearing at the end of the path—praise the Man Jesus—I find myself on the horns of a dilemma. You see, we read Wolves of the Calla nearly a year and a half ago, but I’ve left it unreviewed for a myriad of reasons. Actually . . . no, that’s not entirely true. For some idiotic reason, I began the silly practice of delaying reviews on buddy reads until all, or at least most my friends were finished reading. This delay tactic, commonly referred to as the Delee effect (heh), inevitably led to leaving things unreviewed, unrated, or posting half-assed teasers, which ultimately led to my own demise as a reviewer. Although, to be perfectly honest, unlike Jake Chambers, it wasn’t all that far of a fall . . . but I digress. The point that I’m trying to make is this: As our epic journey together draws to a conclusion, the time for delays is over. It’s time to put up or shut up: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://goo.gl/bL2kbp">goo.gl/bL2kbp</a><br><br>Time to put that elephantine memory to the test. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496757428i/22949655._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hey Rocky, watch me pull a rabbit out of my hat!<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496757428i/22949656.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Wrong hat O.O  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>When last we checked in on Roland’s ka-tet they had just escaped from Oz—yeah, the story gets stranger by the book. Or, if you bothered to read the controversial <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12341557.The_Wind_Through_the_Keyhole__The_Dark_Tower___4_5_" title="The Wind Through the Keyhole (The Dark Tower, #4.5) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Wind Through the Keyhole</a> novel in the proper order, then you last read of the group seeking shelter from a Starkblast, and spending a little more time reminiscing over Roland’s past—yeah, it’s never enough. Either way, the start of our story here sees our fearless ka-tet back along the Path of the Beam, drawing ever nearer to the Dark Tower, until they’re accosted by some townsfolk seeking help.<br><br>The locals tell of some strange goings-on in their home town of Calla Bryn Sturgis. They describe a place that has been blessed with an inordinate amount of twin births, but also cursed in that every twenty years or so the “Wolves” ride down from Thunderclap to claim a child, from each set of twins, for their own. The children are eventually returned to their families, once they’ve served their purpose. But whatever horrific things the Wolves do to the poor children transforms them into drooling idiots, or, as the locals would say, renders them “roont.”<br><br>The townsfolk are fortunate to have an early warning system, in the form of a friendly helper robot named Andy, who’s able to predict when the Wolves will arrive. His latest forecast calls for imminent doom, which sends the Calla spiraling into full panic. Most folks are simply too frightened to fight back, but there’s a small group attempting to shame the majority into growing a backbone. They’re fed up with the status quo, and are finally ready to take a stand, no matter the cost, as long as the gunslingers are willing to stand alongside them that is . . .<br><br>This story initially appeared to be yet another diversion to sidetrack our group from their ultimate goal of reaching the Dark Tower. But as Roland explained, even if that’s the case, it’s a gunslinger’s duty to stand up for those who cannot stand on their own. “Stand and be true.” And, as it just so happened, this leg of the journey later proved to be of vital importance. <br><br>This was our first true glimpse at just how bizarre and wide reaching this saga would become. What with Mia’s banquet hall feast *shudders*, Black Thirteen’s creepy monstrous eye, the Unfound Door, the Cave of Voices, going todash, and Pere Callahan’s backstory. The Wolves themselves, along with their outfits and weapons, were oddly curious, but the most shocking event of all occurred in the final act when King kicked a hole in that fourth wall and inexplicably inserted himself directly into the narrative. <br><br>There was just so much to this story—it was quite the kitten-squisher—that the good far exceeded the bad. King’s character development was once again on point, but the gun battles were brief and underwhelming. This was the first time we saw Roland really let loose—he sang and danced a furious commala at the town hall celebration, even “stage-dived like Joey Ramone.” However, all of the wear and tear of his long life’s journey was clearly starting to take it’s toll. Lucky for him, the rest of his ka-tet have developed into fully fledged gunslingers, so they were more than capable of taking up the slack. And with so much treachery afoot, he needed all the help he could get.<br><br>This installment was an absolute pleasure to read with a ka-tet of my very own, which included: Deadpool’s #1 fan, Mr. Unconventional Reviewer himself, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314429034" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeff</a>; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533807128" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Delee</a>, AKA Miss Thaaang was tragically lost at sea 😢; our three church mice: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036858147" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bev</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535425914" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Jason</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1488506574" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Chris</a>; and, lastly, our dinh, the great sage and eminent Dark Tower junkie, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535417525" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Stepheny</a>. <br><br>Cheers, guys. 🍻</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13212016721992158456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3110951696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3110951696" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3110951696?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/18803882-wolves-of-the-calla">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110951696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7171049049464398336">This 5th book in the <i>Dark Tower</i> series was "the worst" for me so far.<br/><br/>The Ka-tet arrive at the valley town of Calla Bryn Sturgis. The town, at least in my mind, is very Wild West-ish. Lots of farmers and ranchers, a hard life at a sort of frontier. The frontier to what? Well, the Thunderclap - home to "wolves" that steal children in regular intervals from the community (always one of a set of twins). Now, some farmers and ranchers want to rise up while others don't dare. So when the Gunslingers c</span>
  <span id="freeText7171049049464398336" style="display:none">This 5th book in the <i>Dark Tower</i> series was "the worst" for me so far.<br /><br />The Ka-tet arrive at the valley town of Calla Bryn Sturgis. The town, at least in my mind, is very Wild West-ish. Lots of farmers and ranchers, a hard life at a sort of frontier. The frontier to what? Well, the Thunderclap - home to "wolves" that steal children in regular intervals from the community (always one of a set of twins). Now, some farmers and ranchers want to rise up while others don't dare. So when the Gunslingers come through the area, they are asked to help.<br />In the town, our four "heroes" meet Pere Callahan, who turns out to be the priest from King's <b>Salem's Lot</b>. So we get his story in a flashback (all the events since the other novel's end) while the town is explored, people met, secrets uncovered and magical instruments used to visit parallel worlds.<br />Because another story thread here is what happened to a certain bookstore back in our New York after Jake left to join the Ka-tet. Turns out, he - or, rather, some land he owns - is very important in this epic struggle between for the forces of good and evil.<br /><br />Honestly, I liked seeing Father Callahan here, but my god, King could have told his story much more quickly. Just like I enjoyed the mystery of this little town and Andy, but that could have passed more quickly as well. The only thread that had the perfect pacing in my opinion was that of NYC and the bookstore.<br />I am really concerned that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Callahan will become an official member of the Ka-tet, that they're 5 from then on (or 4 if Susannah actually dies), because as interesting as I find Callahan / his appearance in this series, I do NOT see him as part of the Gunslingers <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!<br />But I very much like(d) the mystery of what the wolves actually are. Clearly, they work for the Crimson King, the big bad here, but the big questions was WHAT ARE THEY EXACTLY? You know that feeling when reading a Sherlock Holmes story and people believe in magic and stuff and you are following the clues to find a reasonable explanation? It's a bit like that - only, you can't be sure magic ISN'T involved.<br /><br />The further puzzle pieces we got - such as the significance of the numbers, more about the directive in the tech, why the wolves took the children (and returning them mentally retarded), the connection between the worlds, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mia and the pregnancy,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> the black Maerlyn ball as well as those corporations frequently mentioned both in the universe's past and NYC's present - were all very fascinating once again.<br /><br />Like I said before, this was too drawn out, even for me, even for a SK novel. Callahan's story as well as the preparation of the valley town could have been told much more quickly and it would still have had all the information and suspense. I sincerely considered deducting a star because it was the worst in all the books of the series so far. <br />Then again, I'm still enjoying the romp through the multiverse, I am still discussing intensely all kinds of theories with my buddy-reader, SK still fascinates me with details such as different bodily features displayed by different personalities of one and the same body (there are scientific studies about this kind of phenomenon where a person's one personality is blind while another isn't, or a person whose's one personality has diabetes while the other hasn't), the people keep me engaged (I either roll my eyes at them or want to kill them, usually) and once there is action, there is no time to breathe. <br /><br />And then there was this cliffhanger. My god, SK is cruel! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew there would be SOMETHING happening with / to Susannah because of the child / Mia, but THIS?! Sheesh! I'm hoping, despite the ominous title of the next book, that there is a way for Mia to leave Susannah's body or that ONLY Mia is killed and Susannah therefore freed from this personality when the "chap" is born. I mean, it was said several times that the kid will kill its mother most likely. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Not to mention the introduction of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[SK himself within his own book series. I had known about this but fuck me, that is a weird (and risky) choice <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! I won't continue with the series right away, maybe only on Monday, but I'm glad I don't have to wait for the next volume to be published as that would be torture. I'm obsessing over the story and its details so I guess there is no reason to rate this lower after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7171049049464398336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_63422066" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63422066" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63422066?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=books-i-own-to-read">books-i-own-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=on-deck">on-deck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63422066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17706690970767198666">I didn't really realize until I'd picked up this book that I was kind of in a reading funk for a bit. Either that, or this book is just that good. Either way, I had a new life of reading when I picked up Wolves of the Calla. I was sucked right back into the path of the Dark Tower, right along one of the 6 beams. And it's not just sucked in, but I was able to pick back up after a year or two with only my rusty memory of the previous 5 (counting Wind through the Keyhole) books. <br/><br/>Wolves is just what</span>
  <span id="freeText17706690970767198666" style="display:none">I didn't really realize until I'd picked up this book that I was kind of in a reading funk for a bit. Either that, or this book is just that good. Either way, I had a new life of reading when I picked up Wolves of the Calla. I was sucked right back into the path of the Dark Tower, right along one of the 6 beams. And it's not just sucked in, but I was able to pick back up after a year or two with only my rusty memory of the previous 5 (counting Wind through the Keyhole) books. <br /><br />Wolves is just what I needed and as much as it moves the plot forward, there's plenty more "stories" to be told. It's not quite as much of a stall as in that last book, Wizard and Glass, but it's quite lengthy. But yet again, as in W&amp;G, I loved every minute of it. Back stories have consistently been my favorite parts and King has a gift for backstory and every character has one, that's why they're so rich and why you care so much when they get ripped away from you. In Wolves I was pretty into both the past and the present, you could count them equal. <br /><br />I'd heard things about this book, that's it's sub-par compared to the previous books, but I didn't find that to be the case. I had a great time and only wanted more. Some commentary on the ending: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I did think the ending was a bit anti-climactic, but then again we were warned previously that when guns get pulled out, it can all be over in a few minutes. I expected, however, a bit more. All the lead up with how terrible the wolves are and then it's over with hardly a casualty. Then again, this just shows how studly the gunslingers are. I also enjoyed that the planning really did pay off for them. All the time researching and listening to stories and they really were able to prepare well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I can't leave this review without pointing out the dialect. I think that's one of the greatest parts of this book. I wanted to use it with everyone around me, it sets such a great ambiance about the area and brings you right into it, yer bugger!<br /><br />Well played sai King, I can't wait for more. I'd forgotten the face of my father by waiting so long to reenter the path. Thankee sai for this reminder.<br /><br />4.5 out of 5 Stars (Just under W&amp;G and TW)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17706690970767198666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1894540545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894540545" />
    <a title="Jen from Quebec :0)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0"><img alt="Jen from Quebec :0)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488084323p2/4911921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894540545?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen from Quebec :0)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen from Quebec :0)" href="/user/show/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0">Jen from Quebec :0)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/656420.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=aty-challenge">aty-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=king">king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=horror-aff-tbr-challenge-books">horror-aff-tbr-challenge-books</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894540545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16474300886660094661">OH RIZA! I think this might be my favorite (so far) of all the Dark Tower series of books....which says a lot.<br/><br/>If you were to combine a Western film with the TV show LOST with Back to the Future with a Horror film, you would *almost* have the vibe achieved here. There is hardly anything I can say that will not spoil at least PART of the book, so I will simply continue to sing its praises. <br/><br/>That ENDING! King continues to BLOW MY MIND. The way that EVERYTHING he has ever written seems to somehow ser</span>
  <span id="freeText16474300886660094661" style="display:none">OH RIZA! I think this might be my favorite (so far) of all the Dark Tower series of books....which says a lot.<br /><br />If you were to combine a Western film with the TV show LOST with Back to the Future with a Horror film, you would *almost* have the vibe achieved here. There is hardly anything I can say that will not spoil at least PART of the book, so I will simply continue to sing its praises. <br /><br />That ENDING! King continues to BLOW MY MIND. The way that EVERYTHING he has ever written seems to somehow serve the Dark Tower? Incredible. <br /><br />The tone of this one (despite all the battle and death) was more light-hearted than the last book, and you fall in love with Roland and his ka-tet all over again. Also, having FATHER CALLAHAN FROM 'SALEM'S LOT' join the cast of characters is wickedly awesome. <br /><br />WARNING= do not read if you haven't read the previous 4 books or you'll be *ahem*...LOST. 5 Stars, if it do ya.-Jen from Quebec :0)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16474300886660094661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1696785233284279825">Stephen King’s Dark Tower series is an epic with few peers.<br/><br/>The first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower___1_' title='The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, #1) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gunslinger</a>, was first published in 1982 and the final installment, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5091.The_Dark_Tower__The_Dark_Tower___7_' title='The Dark Tower (The Dark Tower, #7) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Tower</a>, came out 22 years later.<br/><br/>This one, the fifth in the series, was first published in 2003. By this time SK had built up speed and was cruising towards the finish and truth be told, this is my favorite so far.<br/><br/>After I read the Gunslinger I conceded that I was on the outside looking in, that I was missing the punch line to a story loved by h</span>
  <span id="freeText1696785233284279825" style="display:none">Stephen King’s Dark Tower series is an epic with few peers.<br><br>The first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower___1_" title="The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gunslinger</a>, was first published in 1982 and the final installment, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5091.The_Dark_Tower__The_Dark_Tower___7_" title="The Dark Tower (The Dark Tower, #7) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Tower</a>, came out 22 years later.<br><br>This one, the fifth in the series, was first published in 2003. By this time SK had built up speed and was cruising towards the finish and truth be told, this is my favorite so far.<br><br>After I read the Gunslinger I conceded that I was on the outside looking in, that I was missing the punch line to a story loved by hundreds of thousands. When, years later, I picked up the story again in 1987’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_" title="The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Drawing of the Three</a>, I was finally ready to pick up what King was throwing down and I was all in after that.<br><br>The Wolves of the Calla describes Roland and his Ka-tet as they take on the role of Western saviors for a town that has been beset for generations by mysterious riders who come in and abduct children. Stephen King’s use of the western template is masterful, as is his continued and inspired world building in this great American fantasy.<br><br>While this is an engrossing tale told by a great storyteller, it is King’s great design and ambition that are on full display here as he draws from popular culture, myth, legend, fantasy and literature to create a tapestry of unsurpassed detail and complexity.<br><br>He’s rolling, so I’m on to the next one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576796856i/28639176.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <span id="freeText10703846585338815987" style="display:none">I absolutely LOVED this! The ka-tet get to be actual gunslingers in this story. We find out more about North Central Positronics and it's links to Eddie's, Jake's and Susannah's New York's , as well as Father Callahan. We find out how the Dark Tower is as relevant to their world as Roland's although it goes by a different name. We meet Andy, find about about the Wolves..I didn't see the Big Reveal about them until I was told.. it is a testament to King's skill that we don't get to the actual showdown in this book until the very final chapter. The entire book is just building up the detail and cranking up the pressure. And did we get any nearer to the Dark Tower?<br />This was a pivotal book here in terms of the series because King has to start bringing his series together now (only 2 books to go) and to my mind he does an upstanding job. One little intrigue for those of you who haven't read it to ponder and for those who have read it to enjoy: loved the idea of the sneetches!<br />If you haven't guessed by now: Recommended!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4889718170864016254">These books become weirder and weirder with each volume, and this one is the weirdest so far.<br/><br/>To say that I didn't enjoy Wolves of the Calla would be a lie, but the book was too long. Though I love King when he writes big books, but this one was unnecessarily huge and 150-200 pages could have been cut off. This is one of the cases when King turns wordy.<br/><br/>Nevertheless, the book was entertaining and the characters were great, especially Jake, whose character-arc evolve dramatically but powerfully. <br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText4889718170864016254" style="display:none">These books become weirder and weirder with each volume, and this one is the weirdest so far.<br /><br />To say that I didn't enjoy Wolves of the Calla would be a lie, but the book was too long. Though I love King when he writes big books, but this one was unnecessarily huge and 150-200 pages could have been cut off. This is one of the cases when King turns wordy.<br /><br />Nevertheless, the book was entertaining and the characters were great, especially Jake, whose character-arc evolve dramatically but powerfully. <br /><br />I loved meeting once again that character from 'Salem's Lot. His character and story were so much fun and terrifying. <br /><br />And lastly, I had some issues with the last act. I wanted something mind-blowing to take place, alas, I wasn't satisfied.<br /><br />Very good one but not great, but highly-recommended.</span>

<div id="review_1736742611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736742611" />
    <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez"><img alt="Andre Gonzalez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546573233p2/53583787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736742611?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre Gonzalez" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez">Andre Gonzalez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736742611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14285785994934849596">This was a refreshing return to the story of the Ka-Tet and their journey. After what felt like thousands of pages of flashbacks and backstory in Wizard & Glass and Wind Through the Keyhole, Wolves of the Calla returns to Roland and friends in their quest for the Dark Tower. There is so much drama throughout book five, leading up to an exciting ending that leaves you desperate to start the next book right away (which I did!). This book almost feels like a reintroduction of sorts to the main char</span>
  <span id="freeText14285785994934849596" style="display:none">This was a refreshing return to the story of the Ka-Tet and their journey. After what felt like thousands of pages of flashbacks and backstory in Wizard &amp; Glass and Wind Through the Keyhole, Wolves of the Calla returns to Roland and friends in their quest for the Dark Tower. There is so much drama throughout book five, leading up to an exciting ending that leaves you desperate to start the next book right away (which I did!). This book almost feels like a reintroduction of sorts to the main characters and sets up a final two books to the series that is surely to be a page turner til the end!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14285785994934849596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340836156" href="/book/show/815435.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,
