        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190700715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1969976716865166678">8.5/10<br/> <br/>Another stonking effort from the Dark Tower series in a book that has left me drooling at the prospect of what the last two books hold. Initially it seemed like a slow read, this might not be so much the book as external factors making me unable to get chance to read it, and it plodded along and then all of a sudden I was swept up with it all and was engrossed and the last few hundred pages flew by. I would go as far as saying this is in my top two DT books but the slowness of the start m</span>
  <span id="freeText1969976716865166678" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /> <br />Another stonking effort from the Dark Tower series in a book that has left me drooling at the prospect of what the last two books hold. Initially it seemed like a slow read, this might not be so much the book as external factors making me unable to get chance to read it, and it plodded along and then all of a sudden I was swept up with it all and was engrossed and the last few hundred pages flew by. I would go as far as saying this is in my top two DT books but the slowness of the start means that it can’t pip “The Drawing of the Three” for me but there were plenty of positives that would mean I would gladly look forward to re-reading this in my, inevitable, series re-read.<br /> <br />The nuts and bolts of the plot was basically the Gunslingers defending a helpless village from invaders who would take their children. This is a very basic view of the main plot but that isn’t the main attraction here. All the sub stories are what adds to the story here and make for a great read. I’d read some negative reviews of the story saying it took too long and was all filler but I would disagree with the filler part of that argument and say all the extra bits, whilst maybe at first glance, don’t appear to add anything to the story but when the whole thing is looked at it’s clear that they add to the tale overall and make it a great story. I feel reading some of King’s other works first may have helped, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">'Salem's Lot</a> as there is a main character drawn straight from that novel but I’ve never come across due to me never reading that one yet.<br /> <br />The ending leaves it open as to where the story can go but I’ll be keen to read the next book and see what comes from the ending of this book. Overall, a really good read adding to a series that is slowly climbing up my list of all-time favourites.<br /> <br />If you like this try: “The Ecstasy of Gold” by Metallica</span>
  <a data-text-id="1969976716865166678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16797676893837872018">There are a few things that are taking up residence in my head that I can't get into here without blowing the lid off the series as a whole, but woooo-weeee, cowboy (or girl!) it's a doozy! <br/><br/>*giggles and rubs his hands together and is NOT at all surprised that the extended TV show that was supposed to DO THIS SERIES JUSTICE had been pulled* <br/><br/>So, who out there wants to see a wild mashup of westerns, fantasies, horrors, and science fiction?<br/><br/>*crickets*<br/><br/>What? Just me? No. Obviously not just me. But let'</span>
  <span id="freeText16797676893837872018" style="display:none">There are a few things that are taking up residence in my head that I can't get into here without blowing the lid off the series as a whole, but woooo-weeee, cowboy (or girl!) it's a doozy! <br /><br />*giggles and rubs his hands together and is NOT at all surprised that the extended TV show that was supposed to DO THIS SERIES JUSTICE had been pulled* <br /><br />So, who out there wants to see a wild mashup of westerns, fantasies, horrors, and science fiction?<br /><br />*crickets*<br /><br />What? Just me? No. Obviously not just me. But let's add one little detail, my friend number 19. Or should we also add my other friend 99? Or is it 1999? As in, we're gonna party like it's 1999? Or shall we draw back the curtain in the emerald tower and take a good long look at that Dodge Caravan?<br /><br />Muahahahahahahaha<br /><br />I LOVE a good in-joke. I especially love great popular references used by a great writer who is just as much a FAN of popular culture as he is a creator of so much of it. Gimmie that Snitch! Oh, it must have been made by this fellow named Harry Potter...<br /><br />Honestly, I didn't really have ANY clue as to what this book was REALLY supposed to be about when I first picked it up years ago. A big battle on the way to the Dark Tower? Yeah, sure, it is that, but when you start making the world super thin and the todash keeps sending you to New York City and you wish you had a godlike florist to protect the universe from zombies, vampires, and thugs who terrorize bookstore owners, you've got to start wondering why the WOLVES on the edge of End-World are such a mystery. And they are.<br /><br />And I cry beg your pardon, but I LOVE me a good cyborg, thank ye sai.<br /><br />The first time I read this book, I thought it was pretty fine. A bit long in the tooth with padre Calahan, mayhap, but once I'm in on the joke, I like it ALL just fine, now. <br /><br />Bravo, Mr. King. Bravo.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11030834947871479653">And one day I just woke up<br/>And the wolves were all there<br/>Wolves in the piano<br/>Wolves underneath the stairs<br/>Wolves inside the hinges<br/>Circling round my door<br/>At night inside the bedsprings<br/>Clicking cross the floor<br/>I still don’t know how they found me<br/>I’ll never know quite how<br/>I still can’t believe they heard me<br/>I was howling out that loud<br/> - Josh Ritter, great American singer/songwriter<br/><br/>This book works fine as. John Wayne western featuring twin-separating wolves. It was nice to catch up with ol’ Father Callahan,</span>
  <span id="freeText11030834947871479653" style="display:none">And one day I just woke up<br />And the wolves were all there<br />Wolves in the piano<br />Wolves underneath the stairs<br />Wolves inside the hinges<br />Circling round my door<br />At night inside the bedsprings<br />Clicking cross the floor<br />I still don’t know how they found me<br />I’ll never know quite how<br />I still can’t believe they heard me<br />I was howling out that loud<br /> - Josh Ritter, great American singer/songwriter<br /><br />This book works fine as. John Wayne western featuring twin-separating wolves. It was nice to catch up with ol’ Father Callahan, too, although too much of the book was dedicated to his story. The beginning and the end of the book were my favorite parts, but it felt really jumbled and too wordy in the middle. Sometimes it felt like Salem’s Lot 2 was sandwiched between Wolves of the Calla. There’s some goofy robot named sandy, too. It was nice to be back on the path to the Tower, and the story progresses just fine. I’m enjoying the weird turn this series is taking. Each book gets progressively weirder so I’m, you know, excited to finish this thing. I’m not jumping yo and down and chomping at the bit in excitement, but I’m looking forward to pressing on to the next book. I’m also not chomping at the bit because I’m not at horse. Maybe I’m jumping up and down though. Maybe I am right now as I’m typing this out on my phone. You’ll never know, will you? <br /><br />These days I’m reading too many books at once and writing less reviews. I need to flip that and read less books at once and write more reviews. I’m gotta did myself out of this fantasy series pit I’ve found myself stuck in lately. I’m mixing in some other stuff, too. I’ll keep doing that. Maybe I will. You’ll never know, will you?<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3043822977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3043822977" />
    <a title="Gary K Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92857550-gary-k-bibliophile"><img alt="Gary K Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554731392p2/92857550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3043822977?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary K Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary K Bibliophile" href="/user/show/92857550-gary-k-bibliophile">Gary K Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3043822977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14310698283962894648">Wolves of the Calla is book 6 of my 20’19’ Dark Tower odyssey (and book 5 of the series). As with my other reviews this is just a series of observations rather than a full review.<br/> * “[go then] There are other worlds than these”. This quote from Jake going back to the first book.... plays a big factor in this book. <br/> * I have not read Salem’s Lot - it’s been on my TBR list for a while. Nevertheless I enjoyed the crossover quite a lot.<br/> * Going back in time to stop the assassination of JFK... becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText14310698283962894648" style="display:none">Wolves of the Calla is book 6 of my 20’19’ Dark Tower odyssey (and book 5 of the series). As with my other reviews this is just a series of observations rather than a full review.<br /> * “[go then] There are other worlds than these”. This quote from Jake going back to the first book.... plays a big factor in this book. <br /> * I have not read Salem’s Lot - it’s been on my TBR list for a while. Nevertheless I enjoyed the crossover quite a lot.<br /> * Going back in time to stop the assassination of JFK... because it represented a watershed moment in history... now what SK book did he expand on that idea? 🤔😀 I recall that he said JFK was the last gunslinger back in The Drawing of the Three<br /> * “Come commala come come commala”. What a fun song. Oh wait... commala means that?? Oh my!<br />* Sneetches - not nearly a fun as the Dr Seuss versions - I really want to mention something else about this, but that would be telling (i.e. a spoiler... I’m using Patrick McGoohan ‘The Prisoner’ speak... technically Eddie’s the Prisoner in this story - right?)<br />* I like it when Roland gets to break from character. Here he gets to sing and dance and meets a lady friend. Good for him.<br />* Jake gets a little time to be a kid, but unfortunately it doesn’t last<br />* More references to Nozz-a-La cola ( I actually prefer Nuka-Cola )<br />* SK does this a lot to me but whenever he mentions a song I know... it gets stuck in my head for hours... whether it be [Back in the] New York Groove or Someone Saved My Life Tonight (or going back a few books... Velcro Fly)<br />* Lots of pleasantries exchanged in this one “Say thankee” and “Thankee Sai” haha <br />* I find it very interesting the blending of old and new technology in this world. This is true of all the books, but this one in particular. <br />* Not that it was a big deal but since I read ‘Wind Through the Keyhole’ first I had a much better understanding of what was special about ironwood and ghostwood. It was mentioned in Calla but without much elaboration <br />* The Tale of Gray Dick was interesting and I liked the way it fit into the storyline.<br />* Black 13 was wicked cool. Also, going Todash made for some interesting storylines <br />* The final battle was epic <br /><br />Overall it was very entertaining- on to book 6!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14310698283962894648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826204222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826204222" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826204222?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780743533522" href="/book/show/528084.Wolves_of_the_Calla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826204222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7737701934825159806">There's a lot going on here. Luckily, it has the page count so nothing feels rushed. Because there's a new character (really an old one if you read a lot of King) and his backstory, and travel between worlds, and a demonic fetus, and a child-stealing evil to vanquish... Plenty to keep me avidly listening through 22 discs of audiobook.<br/><br/>That new-but-now character is Father Callahan, late of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot' title=''Salem's Lot by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>'Salem's Lot</a>. I wasn't exactly clamoring to see this guy again, and I doubt very many other people were. But </span>
  <span id="freeText7737701934825159806" style="display:none">There's a lot going on here. Luckily, it has the page count so nothing feels rushed. Because there's a new character (really an old one if you read a lot of King) and his backstory, and travel between worlds, and a demonic fetus, and a child-stealing evil to vanquish... Plenty to keep me avidly listening through 22 discs of audiobook.<br /><br />That new-but-now character is Father Callahan, late of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">'Salem's Lot</a>. I wasn't exactly clamoring to see this guy again, and I doubt very many other people were. But here he is, and you know what? His story is one of the most compelling things about this book. I really like Callahan as a character, and his story only made me like him more.<br /><br />For me, it was interesting to Roland at work as an actual Gunslinger. It's a side of the role we haven't really seen before. Sure, we've seen bits and pieces, but never the whole thing all in one time and place. It's kind of cool to see Roland's politician side, and he puts it to very good use here in winning over the townsfolk. It's kind of interesting to me how the vast majority of the book is planning, while the actual battle goes relatively quickly. That was also the case in the previous book, and it must be intentional. Maybe King doesn't particularly like drawn out action scenes, but it also seems like something that would define a Gunslinger: the battle is all in the planning. I do not shoot with my hand; he who shoots with his hand has forgotten the face of his father. I shoot with my mind. Maybe this will make the book slow going for some, but I was fascinated the whole way.<br /><br />Speaking of, I want to make an aside to specifically say how much I liked that, though there's a divide in the town, the ones who are against accepting Roland's help are not portrayed as being in any way evil. Sure, they're wrong, but from their limited point of view they have legitimate concerns: if Roland and his ka-tet are unable to stop the Wolves from stealing half of their children, the Wolves might steal all of them, and raze the town, and kill all left standing. It would have been so easy to show them as stupid, as evil, as traitors. But by and large, they aren't, and that's a far more difficult thing to write.<br /><br />The todash elements are also very interesting. It's the major fantasy element in this book, and I liked that there was more than one way to go todash. Revisiting New York at this point was actually kind of jarring, as well it should have been. And even more so when the vagrant dead show up. <br /><br />At this point, is each book in the series going to be better than the last? I have no problem with that, though that's an increasingly difficult task.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7737701934825159806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2714464799" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2714464799" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11818290-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476068938p2/11818290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2714464799?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/11818290-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444723489" href="/book/show/12697885-wolves-of-the-calla">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2714464799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12953850841135637190">13/2 - I loved how meta this whole book was - references to <i>Harry Potter</i>, King himself, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot' title=''Salem's Lot by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>'Salem's Lot</a> (don't read this till you've read that or you'll be totally spoiled), and <i>Star Wars</i> abound. One of my favourite literary devices is when a character breaks the fourth wall or there are references to our 'world' in the story (one of the only lines I know off the top of my head from the TV show <i>Charmed</i> is from a scene where the sisters are in a mausoleum and Piper quips "Where's Buffy when you need</span>
  <span id="freeText12953850841135637190" style="display:none">13/2 - I loved how meta this whole book was - references to <i>Harry Potter</i>, King himself, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">'Salem's Lot</a> (don't read this till you've read that or you'll be totally spoiled), and <i>Star Wars</i> abound. One of my favourite literary devices is when a character breaks the fourth wall or there are references to our 'world' in the story (one of the only lines I know off the top of my head from the TV show <i>Charmed</i> is from a scene where the sisters are in a mausoleum and Piper quips "Where's Buffy when you need her?") and King does that a lot in this book.<br /><br />I liked how Jake is starting to grow up and has more responsibility within the group - getting his own mission that only he could have completed and the information he gathered was vital to the overall mission of saving the town. I was a bit annoyed by what happened with Susannah because it feels like she just can't catch a break and I thought <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we were done with that kind of plot with the merging of Detta and Odetta at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5094.The_Drawing_of_the_Three__The_Dark_Tower___2_" title="The Drawing of the Three (The Dark Tower, #2) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Drawing of the Three</a> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm interested to see where the plot goes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5093.Song_of_Susannah__The_Dark_Tower___6_" title="Song of Susannah (The Dark Tower, #6) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Song of Susannah</a>. I was surprised by the ending, I thought it was going to be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a lot more bloody than it was. I thought there might be a main character death, or at least a serious maiming, plus a whole pile of the townspeople - it was much more triumphant than I ever expected (I figured they would win, but I thought it would be a very bittersweet victory for everyone involved). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was saddened by the fact that the ka-tet were hiding things from each other and thought Roland would (should) make more of an effort to bring everyone back together once he realised what was happening and the possible consequences of there being distance between the group (the whole 'leave it up to ka' always irritates me the same as 'it's in God's hands' does in real life). Once again Oy was a star who didn't get enough screen time. I don't know what the plot of <i>The Song of Susannah</i> is, except guessing that it's got a lot to do with Susannah, but I really want Oy to have a more central role, to really do something like he did in <i>The Wastelands</i> (except, of course, he's not allowed to die). Can't wait to get started on <i>The Song of Susannah</i> as soon as I finish my current series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9401317.Foundation__Foundation___1_" title="Foundation (Foundation, #1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12953850841135637190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874868319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874868319" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874868319?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/33977904-wolves-of-the-calla">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874868319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10172197515366066185">I didn't think it was possible to be any more in love with this series than I already was. But with each book I reread, my love for it just keeps growing. I've become so invested in these characters and their journey that it feels like they've become a part of me. <br/><br/>I had forgotten a lot of the details of the story so at times it's almost like I'm on the Dark Tower journey again for the first time. And it's truly a magical experience. I feel like now that I'm a bit older, I'm able to truly appreci</span>
  <span id="freeText10172197515366066185" style="display:none">I didn't think it was possible to be any more in love with this series than I already was. But with each book I reread, my love for it just keeps growing. I've become so invested in these characters and their journey that it feels like they've become a part of me. <br /><br />I had forgotten a lot of the details of the story so at times it's almost like I'm on the Dark Tower journey again for the first time. And it's truly a magical experience. I feel like now that I'm a bit older, I'm able to truly appreciate the epicness of this tale. <br /><br />And I'm noticing so many details that I hadn't before. I hadn't read as many King books the first time I read the series and it's truly stunning how he has woven in his other works and characters from them. <br /><br />This book is definitely one of my favourites out of the series. I love the secrets and the trickery that are present throughout. But most of all, I love getting to see the gunslingers in action and that stunning final showdown. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10172197515366066185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CXgNGondSyw5J5crJiB0DgHgvdJvUYh16sO+MFgq3cXiOqyTGgR+r132zekhvAmeJuUBAVu2ehAd6Oe+1Pz/1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4LeuvM/ZcdIeFeLRBdx6FzdBvad/45PAsOlhh8g/fJIL9Q81XABEUXrEuBMCQAeHEEQBdEsEYaVHwjgJROlegw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,326
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1816099263117115838">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText1816099263117115838" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1816099263117115838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
